Electric shavers ---------------- If you buying an electric shaver for the first time, skip this section and read the next Electric shavers basically come in 2 types - Rotary (philips norelco) & foil (braun & panasonic) Rotaries are good for cutting longer hairs let us say you skip to shave over a holiday then start shaving on Monday morning. Foil shavers are faster and easier to adapt to, since they are very much like your gilette razors, but there are a few downsides - foils are difficult to clean since the hair gets trapped in the inner chamber and foil shavers give you more burn compared to rotary blades. This is a foil shaver About Panasonic 5-Blade Shaving System --------------------------------------- Shave Quality : Rotary shavers have never been able to offer me the kind of close shave that I have been able to get through this particular foil shaver. I have tried cheaper foil shavers before, but almost always it has left me with razor burns. East of use : The flexible heads make it very easy to shave around the neck. If you are graduating from a Gilette to this one - you will find that this is much easier to adapt to than a rotary shaver. Someone even after 3 years of being with rotary shavers, I still get a bit fearful as I take my rotary shaver around the neck, but not with this Panasonic foil shavers Hygiene & Safety : Why is hygene all the more important in an electric shaver ? You see the blades are so much close to your skin and obviously they do scrape off live matter into an enclosed chamber along with the hair. Now, if you these blades were not to be hypoallergic, they would encourage growth of these live matter along with bacteria. But the Panasonic 5 blade shaver comes with hypoallergic blades which ward off growth of such bacteria and keep it clean, of course you have to do your due diligence of rinsing the blades in hot water and cleaning it. Self Cleaning Comes with a Sonic vibrate cleaner which create a pulsating action when you hold it under water - it will clean the micro follicles in the shaver. Other Good features : Not too worried about the other features such as battery life - it is not a mobile phone to be held in hand for hours together - almost ALL the shavers in the market today offer a charge to last for a couple of days, which is good enough. -- Another important thing is to dual voltage operability if you travel to Asia/Europe and this shaver can work with dual voltages -- 14000 rpm : the faster the foil vibrates, the more efficient it is in giving a clean shave on the very first run and this is currently the fastest in the market Comparison to Braun : Sorry, I do not have a clue as to how Braun shavers are - they make foil shavers too. Remington and Philips make rotary shavers. But I did do some research on foil replacements and found that Panasonic foils are less expensive compared to Braun foils - obviously Panasonic shavers will cost a lot less to maintain over the years Value for Money : An investment in a good electric shaver really pays over time - no price is small to wake up each day in the morning, get a clean shave in a minute or two and walk out confidently. Not with a $20 shaver or even the most expensive rotary shaver will you get this kind of a feeling - I can tell you from my own personal experience. I did not realize this until I started using the a quality foil shaver like this. If you think of the fact that you spend about $5 for a razor every 2-4 weeks - which adds up to $100 per year - this is a good buy.

  45. This 5-blade Panasonic LV61 shaver is like the Rolls-Royce of shavers, it's definitely pricey, but what a fine fine cutting instrument. How does it compare to a Braun Pulsonic (model 9595/790cc)? ============================================================ I had a Braun Pulsonic many, many years ago when they first came out and indeed that is a great shaver with a really long battery life. It had this \\"sterilizing\\" charger, but you had to routinely buy the alcohol-based cleaning-solution packs. The trimmer had a long reach and the ergonomics were spot on. The travel case was a chintsy, opaque plastic hard-case with a cleaning comb. I always thought the \\"sterilizing\\" charger was a bit overrated --- you don't need it, if you're only recharging it once every 2-3 weeks anyways, what good does sterilizing it that one time really offer? Frankly though, I've used electric razors some 25 years, well before these \\"sterilizing\\" gizmos came out... How does it compare to the 4-blade Panasonic LA63? ==================================================== The 4-blade LA63 feels slightly heavier and top-heavy. Though mine still works great, it feels cheaper in quality from grip to aesthetics. The button to turn on the shaver is \\"chrome-plastic-coated\\" and has worn off to reveal some white-plastic. The trimmer is fairly short and does not give you the reach the Braun does. If you're holding a mirror and trying to get the fuzz on the back of your neck, it's pretty difficult; much easier with my old Braun. [Update 10-8-11: I went and did the 'balance it on your finger trick\\" and the LA63 will not balance even with my finger near the very end, it is very top-heavy. I did the same thing with the LV61 and it will balance on my finger near the midpoint of the shaver, meaning it is very balanced and that explains why it just feels better in your hand.] No fancy \\"sterilizing\\" system, just an AC charger. The case is actually a nice black leather soft-case with a plastic cap for the shaver head. I will state that the 4-blade LA63 shaves closer than the Braun. What's improved with the 5-blade LV61 over the 4-blade LA63? ============================================================== The 5-blade Panasonic LV61 is a little lighter and better balanced [see Update note above]. The quality is leagues ahead of the LA63. It simply feels more elegant, solid and less plastic-y. The button to turn on the shaver feels like real metal. One nice improvement is that there's a \\"lock-ring\\" for the power button such that it prevents the shaver from accidentally turning on if you shove it in your suitcase. [Update: the 4-blade LA63 does have a sliding \\"lock-button\\" to keep it from accidentally turning on when shoved in a suitcase] The trimmer is identical and visual LED indicators are the same. The leather travel soft-case and protective cap, etc is also the same. The AC charger has a different part number and I haven't dared try to see if the older one would work, not at these prices! Another improvement is the 5-minute fast-charge. One complaint about the Panasonics over the Braun is that the Braun can be plugged into the AC charger and can be used at the same time. Both Panasonics will not turn on while plugged-in. This is really only a concern for \\"always late\\" people like myself when you are late for work, go to use the electric shaver and it is out of battery. With my Braun, I could just plug in and use it. The 4-blade LA63 would barely have enough power after 5-minutes (from empty) to truly give me a work-presentable shave....time to get out the disposable razor. [Small Update 10-8-2011: When you charge the 4-blade LA63 overnight, when it is done, it will brightly glow and blink \\"100%\\" forever until you unplug it. This is only annoying if you are a light sleeper and the blinking LED indicator in a dark room will bother you all night. When you charge the 5-blade LV61, it will glow a solid blue while it is chargingand at some point when it reaches 100%, it stops glowing and turns its blue LED indicators off.] The Shave: ============ The shave on the 5-blade LV61 is as close as any blade razor without drawing blood! I did the chin-stubble test and with this 5-blade LV61, you absolutely cannot feel any stubble, it's an extremely close shave! I almost always draw blood when using a razor and my skin always feels raw. Perhaps my skin is simply used to electric shavers, but I get close shaves that last beyond 5pm, with no mess of shaving cream and no nicks from razors and my skin always feels smooth. Is it closer than my 4-blade LA63? Trying to remember my chin-stubble test for when my LA63 was brand-new, I think both are very close and still better than the Braun. The 5-blade LV61 if anything provides a faster shave (than the Braun). The instructions state the outer foil blades will last 2 years and the main inner blades will last 1 year, but I think that'll vary based on how scruffy you get. For my 4-blade LA63, I believe 8 months is about when I replaced the blades. Note: Currently it seems like replacement blades for the 5-blade LV61 are around $75-$99 or so and not easily found on Amazon (as of this writing) - this may play a small factor in your buying decision. Overall thoughts: ==================== The Braun is the Cadillac. The 4-blade LA63 is the Mercedes. The 5-blade LV61 is the Rolls Royce. You can be just as luxurious in the Mercedes and be perfectly content, but when you want fine-attention to detail, slight improvements here and there, elegance, a nice solid feel, you splurge, sometimes twice the price of a Mercedes, so that you can roll around in style - the Rolls-Royce! [Update: 9-17-12 - While replying to some comments on my review, I decided to read what other people were saying in their reviews. I noticed a few people mention that it was really only 2-blades, since when you pop the cover off, you only see two blades. That is a little misleading. On the shaver are 2 main blades. Inside of the foil that you pop-off, are the other 3 blades. If you measure the distance of where those 2 main blades are, they are a little less than half an inch towards the center of the head. Now if you put the foil back on and use only the very edge of the shaver head (well before you get to the 2 main blades in the center), you will see that it really is a usable blade as it cuts your stubble. So yes, this is indeed a 5-blade shaver and verified.] ######## I originally put this as a comment, but pasting it here since it's applicable ########3 Replacement Foil and Blades report: ========================================= [Update: 12-13-12 - In October, I purchased the replacement outer foil (Part no: WES9171P) and inner blades (Part no: WES9170P) and paid $38 shipped and $21 shipped respectively (I'm a Prime member). I can verify those are indeed the correct part numbers. Note: There is also part no: WES9030P which is the outer foil and inner blades in a COMBO package. Well, as of October 2012, the cheapest I could find WES9030P for on Amazon was $70 shipped. Now, I paid $38+$21 shipped, which is $59 total! And yes, in this case, it is cheaper to buy both separately than getting the combo. Also, note that this puts my replacement interval at ~1 year, definitely NOT the 2 year life that Panasonic puts in the owner's manual. Judging myself as having a lighter stubble/beard growth pattern than most, you will likely want to replace your blades every 8-12 months for optimal shaving results.] [Update: 1-30-15 - You might not find the WES9030P COMBO pack anymore, the new part number, which lists THIS ES-LV61 is WES9032P and is $65 for Amazon Prime as of today's date. So yes, as of 1-30-15 it is now cheaper to buy the COMBO pack - WES9032P ~$65]

  82. This is a remarkable razor, it shaves close, it shaves as good as a blade, it feels good in my hand, it is very fast, and the trimmer works well. But is it really worth $500? Sadly, I have to say no.<br /><br />This is a luxury product. The shaver itself is well built and designed. The handle is exactly the right size for my hand, it fits perfectly. The on off button is surrounded by a lock switch and it's very easy to not put your hand or finger on that button while using the razor (when the on / off switch is pressed for too long, the razor goes into clean mode). The head is massive; it is about the width of two manual razors across and about three manual razors wide. The size is a mixed blessing. On the one hand it covers ground really fast on my face. On the other hand it blocks the trimmer from view and makes it difficult to get into tight places (especially to shave around or trim a beard).<br /><br />Where the luxury ends is the included accessories. The box is hideous. When I spend this kind of money, I absolutely expect to be in awe over the presentation. I should open the box and be amazed by the product. Instead, the razor looks like any other piece of cheap appliance or electronics I've bought. Panasonic should have taken a page from so many other luxury product makers and created a beautiful box worthy of this price. There are $50 razors with better packaging.<br /><br />The included travel case is a joke, cheap nasty vinyl zippered case. At this price point, there should have been a leather case, or neoprene, or fine imitation leather. This is the nastiest vinyl I've ever seen. The AC adapter is decent, it is well built and looks like it will survive long use. I still expect this to be something special, the electrical connector should work better. There is no stand, and no included cleaning supplies. The instructions recommend a cleaning soap that should be in the box.<br /><br />The shave is excellent. I have tried some electric razors and been disappointed. I am a razor and shaving cream man. This machine shaves as close as a razor and shaving cream. It does the job quickly and feels good on my face. It does not give me razor burn. It delivers a close smooth shave all over my face. It does a bad job on longer hairs; the tendency is to pull those hairs as opposed to cutting them (it hurts a lot). Two or three day growth is not a pleasant experience. Razors do not have this problem; they cut hair no matter the length.<br /><br />The trimmer is another mixed deal. On the one hand it works for places like sideburns and light mustache trimming. It really falls down trimming other hair. The cutters point out perpendicular to the shaver with absolutely no protection, it will cut through skin. Shaving the top of my head was a delicate operation. If the hairs get longer than half an inch, the foil won't cut them without pulling. The trimmer has to be used to get these longer hairs and it is very hard to not cut my head, I hesitate to use the trimmer beyond where I can see in the mirror. It does a great job on outer ear hair. This is not a very good tool to use for manscaping. It works fine for the northern parts, but get down to the southern parts and things get a bit more difficult. The trimmer has to be used very carefully and sometimes that big old shaver head goes places you don't want. The foil cutters really don't work very well on the southern most areas, they have a tendency to cut a bit further than you'd like (read bleeding). As delicately as I can put it, the trimmer does a good job on really thick hedges and gets things close enough to finish up with a razor, but don't try the foil head on the final clear cut on those delicate parts. I would imagine that it works pretty well for women, legs, under arms, and lady parts (at least the northern area).<br /><br />The razor works perfectly in the shower. It is completely waterproof and designed to be used wet or dry. It is very easy to dry off afterwards and theunreachable dries easily sitting on the shelf in the bathroom.<br /><br />The battery charges in about 30 minutes. The display panel on the handle shows how long the razor has been used since last charge and the percent charge left. The battery lasts an eternity. There is no need to pack the charger for a one week trip (well unless you are shaving a lot more than just your face). It's probably not a bad idea to use the clear plastic cover for the foil and the travel case when the razor goes into carry on luggage.<br /><br />The value equation, is it really worth $500? When the Braun system is $200 and generally does a good job, the Panasonic seems overpriced. For the level of shave and the waterproof, I would peg this as a $300 razor. Panasonic would have won me over with better packaging, finer accessories, a dedicated website, and some way of making me feel special for buying this expensive device. Instead, it is packaged and represented like any other razor.<br /><br />I have no idea how long the blades will last. The good news, the Panasonic website sells them and they are in the $15 arena (the foils are much more expensive, $60). So if they have to be replaced once per year, that's not too bad. The instructions show a tear down to dispose of the battery. It looks like with a few tools the battery is not hard replace.<br /><br />I love the razor, I hate the price.<br /><br />January 8, 2015 Update: I've used this razor for over three years now. I still love it. I've tried a few other electric razors and keep coming back to this. I've replaced the blades one time, and should have done it way sooner. About once per year is the right time frame. I'm guessing in the three years, I probably would have spent close to that much money on disposable blades and shaving cream - so the deal isn't that bad.unreachable dries easily sitting on the shelf in the bathroom.<br /><br />The battery charges in about 30 minutes.   83. Having recently switched from hot foam to a gel, I was not planning on another switch to cordless electric. However, this one was enough to convince me. When you're thinking of plunking down $500 for a shaver, you may think that you'll get something that plays music and provides a back massage in addition to an excellent shave. However, this shaver (or Shaving System as Panasonic likes to call it) is simplicity itself.<br /><br />The charging unit does not come with a giant black box that takes up five sockets on a outlet strip, but instead it has a small (wider than normal) plug that takes up a single outlet and weights less than several pounds. A Liquid Crystal Display (LCD) provides information about the shaver's current state--how long it's been on, whether it needs cleaning, what percent of charge is left. The shaver has 3 settings--Free (the head swivels left and right up and down, Lock (no swivel) and trim (a little trimmer pops up) that can be changed single handedly. I lock it while going over the flat sides of my face; for around my jaw, to swivel; and for mustache and side burns, to trim. It also has a lock on/off button that I though silly but have come to appreciate. When shaving, it's easy to place your thumb on the on/off switch and accidentally turn it off. By the simple expedient of locking it on and then locking it off there are no accidental start/stops.<br /><br />Perhaps the biggest plus to this shaver is cleaning it. Press the on/off button for 2 seconds or more and it goes into \\"clean mode\\" and starts cleaning itself. Pour in some liquid hand soap right in the top and it gives itself a bubble bath. Rinse it off, and you've got a clear sharp shaver like new. Because it's a wet/dry shaver (for those of you who like to shave in the shower), you can drop it in the tub and it just keeps on buzzing until you pull it out.<br /><br />Now for the main point: How does it shave? It's very smooth; no pulls, and while I have to run over a patch of bristle more than once, my razor shave with hot foam or gel did not do the job as well. The trimmer lets me handle mustache and sideburn trimming along with shaving. It's simple, effective and considerate and worth the long term investment. If you buy something you're going to use everyday, why not get the best?ve with hot foam or gel did not do the job as well.   116. Hitherto trying the Panasonic ES-LV61, I didn't even know manufacturers made $500 electric shavers. $500 you say, that's crazy! Yes, I thought so too until I used the Panasonic. I've primarily been a manual shaver man most of my life, bouncing from the early Mach 3s, to Remingtons, and then my trusty Fusion. My last electric shaver was a $90 Norelco 1150X, which I thought was pricey for a shaver. I had a bad experience with the Norelco, despite being advertised as being able to dry shave, was never able to do so without irritating my sensitive skin. Moreover, I found the Norelco had a tendency to shave off large patches of hair, in a particularly uneven manner. So my faith in electric shavers was shaken until the Panasonic... EXTERIOR DESIGN: The first feature you'll notice about the Panasonic is the particularly strikingly large head, comprising 5-blades. It reminds me of the Mach-3/Quattro/Fusion manual razor wars, where each manufacturer would try to up the other in terms of the number of blades. However on the Panasonic, the 5 blades aren't a gimmick, they do wonders. The blades are encased in a head, which has an easily removable outer casing, which exposes the inner blades for cleaning. Depress two buttons on each side of the head, and the outer casing pops right off. The head freely rotates, though somewhat limited in its side-to-side and back and forth motion. The rotation was more than suitable for my shaving needs. The head also mounts an integrated trimmer which is easily locked into place by a selector mounted below. The shaver is a beautiful gun-metal dark blue, and is not a bright tacky light blue like on the Norelco. The body is finished in a 3/4 slip-resistant & fingerprint resistant material, which is comfortable to hold. The body is also contoured for a comfortable grip. There is a chrome circular selector switch that toggles between operating mode and travel lock mode. Lastly, a display screen with bright blue LED digits showsbattery life, minutes/seconds the shaver was in use (a helpful feature), charge status, etc.. The LED display is very bright, and easy to read, even in a pitch black room. The razor recharges with an AC adapter connected to its base; for the price, I was expecting at least a pedestal/stand of some sort. Oh well. It's a solid, good looking razor. OPERATION: The Panasonic only needs 1 hour charging time, before full operation. A quick 5-10 minute charge will get you maybe 1-2 shaves. The ES-LV61 emits a solid, high pitched whine when in use. The 14,000 cpm and 5 blades is no joke here. I was able to dry shave WITHOUT SKIN IRRITATION. That's a first for me, as I have sensitive skin which I usually have to slap with copious amounts of aftershave following each session. My post dry-shave session was incredible, didn't even feel like I had just shaved. I also tried the Panasonic with a wet-shave, and was able to achieve an amazingly close shave. Remember the old adage that an electric shaver will never be able to replicate the results of a manual blade or razor? The Panasonic completely destroys that adage. I feel as smooth as the proverbial baby's posterior. The Panasonic also allows shaving in the shower. The trimmer works no differently, and I was able to get a smooth trim on my sideburns. The LV61 is also very easy to clean. Add a little dishwashing liquid or liquid soap to the outer blades, hold down the power button to activate the \\"sonic vibration mode\\", at which point the razor self-cleans. I also used a toothbrush to remove some small hairs that had deposited on the base of the inner blades. OVERALL THOUGHTS: Is the Panasonic expensive? Yes, but it certainly lives up to its claims and provides an amazing shave. Cue heavenly music playing from above. Should I buy this LV61 or the more expensive ($100 more MSRP) LV81 shaving system with integrated charging base/cleaning dock? I'd recommend saving yourself $100 and sticking with this LV61, because the integrated sonic vibration mode is more than sufficient to clean the shaver, unless, you're really that lazy. There is one caveat, this LV61 shaver is not interchangeable with the shaver on the LV81 cleaning/docking system; the LV61 is missing three electrodes on the rear of the body which allow charging with the cleaning/docking system. The biggest downside of the Panasonic is that it requires replacement of the blades every 1-2 years, though I expect those who are less hirsute can observe a more lax replacement system. These replacement blades don't come cheap either, at least $50-70 (which is about standard for electric shavers; IIRC, replacement Norelco blades were about that much too). If you want a cost-effective system, stick with manual razors. If you're putting down five benjamins for this system, then replacement blade costs probably aren't going to deter you from making the purchase.

The Panasonic Arc 5 electric shaver provides a close, irritation free shaving experience, and has an efficient and convenient sonic cleaning mode.<br /><br />Control wise the shaver is very simple. It only has one button, the power button. Around the power button is a rotating control to lock the shaver's power button for use when traveling. On the back of the shaver is a sliding switch that has two positions. The first locks the head of the shaver from pivoting, and the second pops out the trimmer for cutting sideburns. There is an illuminated LCD display on the front that lets you know battery status, the length of your shave, when to clean the shaver heads, when to replace the shaver heads, and when the sonic cleaning mode is activated. Included with the shaver is a zippered travel case.<br /><br />The shaver has a rubber back and a nicely shaped handle that makes shaving comfortable. The head of the shaver is rather large though, so it can feel a little top heavy at times. The 5 blades shave very closely, and the freely pivoting head help keep them in close contact with your skin. Indeed, it's probably one of the closest shaves I've ever had, and works just as well my high-end rotary Norelco (I should note that I've only ever shaved with an electric shaver and always shave dry). Additionally, it's very easy on my sensitive skin and leaves behind no redness or sensitivity. The only caveats about its performance are that I have to make multiple passes over my neck, and that it can snag on my hairs a bit when I let my stubble grow out for a few days. Lastly since the head of the shaver is so large it's hard to shave around an intricate goatee or get right under the nose.<br /><br />Cleaning the shaver is very easy. When the cleaning icon comes up on the LCD you simply turn the shaver off, wet the head of the shaver and apply a little liquid hand soap. Next, you press the power button for two seconds to activate the sonic cleaning mode, which runs for 20 seconds. Lastly, you remove the outer foil section, turn on the sonic cleaning mode again and run the shaver under hot water. It cleans the blades and shaver housing very thoroughly.<br /><br />The shaver takes 1 hour to charge, has a 45-minute run time, and a 5-minute quick charge if you need to get a quick shave in and the shaver's battery is dead. That said, it requires several passes and a lot of patience to achieve that clean look and feel (about four minutes, which doesn’t sound like a long time, but believe me, it is longer than you realize). Moreover, if you skip a day, forget it. At least for my hair, which is fairly coarse, so it takes forever to get my head shaved if I skip a day. And if I skip two? I literally cannot use the shaver. I first have to crop it very tightly with hair clippers or shave with a straight razor.<br /><br />Perhaps more troubling is its face shaving capability (or lack thereof), which when you think about it, makes no sense because it was designed for the face rather than the scalp as far as I know. Anyway, I cannot get a clean face shave no matter how much time I spend. For whatever reason, it simply does not give me a clean shave on my cheeks, and shaving my neck is a nightmare. I can move the razor in multiple directions, going back and forth over and over and over, and I STILL cannot get all the hairs on my neck shaven clean. About the only place I can get a clean shave is along my jawline. I therefore suspect that this razor does well with taut skin (skin covering the jaw and scalp), but suffers terribly with skin that is more malleable (along the cheeks and neck, with no hard bone underneath).<br /><br />In sum then, I would give this shaver four stars for its head shaving capability but only two stars for its face shaving ability given that I cannot get a clean shave no matter what I do. That of course is in an absolute sense, but given that this razor also costs $200, it really is a terrible value. Even worse? I just learned that you need to replace the blades every few months, which at the time of writing, cost an additional $64 per replacement. That means I spent $200 up front and can expect continue to spend at least $130 a year keeping fresh blades on the shaver. NOT good news.<br /><br />All of this being said, I will never go back to razor blades, particularly for my head. The fact that I no longer have to worry about slicing a sweet two-inch layer of skin off my scalp any given morning (which is what prompted my purchase to begin with) makes using electric shavers worth the aggravation. However, I will definitely look to an alternative when this one wears out its utility (which may be sooner than later unfortunately – it can only hold a four-day charge now as it is).<br /><br />A couple of final thoughts:<br /><br />1) I suggest not getting lured by some of the bells and whistles of this model that, in my opinion, are of very little value in practice. For example, the digital display of the percent battery remaining is nearly useless. How is a digital display of a blinking 10% battery reserve any more useful than simply having a little LED light turn orange or red when battery power is low? It’s not like this model kicks into power reserve or anything, and you can’t see the readout while you’re shaving anyway, so it's not like you will suddenly know you need to hurry up and finish before the battery dies. Even more interesting is that you cannot operate it while it is plugged in. I suspect this is due to the fact that it is a wet-dry shaver, so it automatically disables function when plugged in. This of course is a nightmare if you did not notice you were low on charge and started shaving, only to have the battery die mid-shave (which unfortunately has happened to me). In fact, in that respect, I think a red LED light on the outside would actually be more useful than a digital readout because you don’t see the readout until you turn on the shaver anyway.<br /><br />2) The lock mechanism is alsouseless in my opinion. I travel a lot, and I take my shaver with me every trip. I have never once used the lock mechanism to prevent it from being turned on accidentally, nor have I ever had it turn on accidentally. I mean, really. What are the odds? You have to pack it in clothes (or something soft) to prevent it from getting banged up in your luggage anyway, so how is it going to get turned on? And at home? Honestly? All you do is turn it off, rinse it off, and set it on your counter to dry. How is it going to turn on by itself just sitting there? Why pay for this feature. I don't know, maybe I'm missing something, but these bells and whistles seem like a way to merely increase the price of the shaver than actually serving any useful purpose.<br /><br />Long and short, I suggest steering clear of buying a more expensive version of a shaver because of seemingly useless bells and whistles. They just are not worth it, at least not the ones that this particular model offers over other more basic models.<br /><br />As for me, I'll grin and bear this purchase until I can no longer, but then I will have to start the search all over. If anyone has any suggestions, I'd love to hear them.useless in my opinion. I travel a lot, and I take my shaver with me every trip. I have never once used the lock mechanism to prevent it from being turned on accidentally, nor have I ever had it turn on accidentally. I mean, really. What are the odds? As I mentioned before, I have always ended up with a 5:00 shadow with any razor/shaver I've ever used. With the Panasonic, come 5:00, my skin is still pretty smooth with almost no stubble. I'm writing this review in the morning having shaved yesterday morning, and my beard is at about the level it would typically be at 5:00 the day before. So the Panasonic has many great features (good battery life, charges quickly, cleans easily, etc.), but the closeness of the shave is unlike any shaver I have used and is what truly sets the Panasonic apart.
  186. If you're reading this you must be thinking about moving over from another brand such as Braun or Remington or moving up from a less expensive Panasonic. You're also probably asking yourself why this shaver is so expensive and do you really have to spend this much money to upgrade.<br />Before delving in to the LV61-A I thought a brief review of the Panny line of linear shavers might be in order:<br /><br /> -- The 3-blade 8103S is the least expensive at about $78 here at Amazon<br />and IMHO offers the best electric shaver value on the market. It delivers a shave I would rate at 4.25 stars out of five.(Note that this model has been replaced by the LT41-K which is almost identical in features.) It is well built, feels solid in the hand and its narrow head makes it extremely maneuverable. This means it's particularly good at getting into tight spots that are hard to reach. All the shavers discussed here are about the same length and weight so the weight missing from this model's head must be in the handle, giving it that solid feel.<br />The feature I look for most in a shaver is a head that pivots from front to back as I find that necessary to do a good job on my neck and jawline. Unfortunately, that feature is missing on this model and the 4-blade models other than the LA63-S. Those models swivel freely from side to side and, for some reason I can't fathom, move up and down as more or less pressure is applied. If you want to stop this movement, however, you can engage the head lock button and get full concentration on your face.<br />The flip side of this missing feature, happily, is a good trimmer. This is because the trimmer is located on the back of the head and the bracket that holds it in place traverses the neck of the shaver, thereby precluding any fore and aft motion of the head. The result is a trimmer of perfect length and better than the other two models discussed here.<br /><br />If you have a light to average beard or are simply satisfied with a good but not spectacular shave at a reasonable cost, IMHO you don't need more than the 8103S. And the fact that this shaver constantly runs neck-to-neck with the Braun 790cc for best-selling linear shaver on Amazon would seem to bear this out.<br /><br /> --The 4-blade LA63-S is considerably more expensive at about $200 as I write this(it is usually less when sold by Amazon but at the moment Amazon seems to be out of stock or just leaving it to third-party sellers). This model has a huge head that pivots freely from front to back and side to side. The handle feels light and plasticy and the head large and heavy. This top-heaviness makes it feel rather clumsy and unergonomic. Worse, the front to back pivot motion I consider so<br />important is TOO free because it`s not well damped. It sort of reminds me of a rolling pin over dough!<br />This shaver is about .5 inches longer than the LV61 and that length (which I consider a disadvantage in ergonomics and handling) is all in the head, which stands taller than the LV61 and makes it appear larger though it really is not. Oddly, the bigger heads on the LA63 and LV61 result in shorter trimmers than the 8103S. This is because the trimmers are once again built into the back of the head, but because of the pivoting action must be built above the neck of the shaver. This leaves less space in which to fit the trimmer and appears to be a design necessity rather than a fault.<br /><br />The LA63 delivers a shave I would rate at 4.5 stars but misses the mark in ergonomics, quality of feel and, most of all, maneuverability. I ditched mine after just two months of use in favor of the Braun Series 7,<br />which I liked much more. But this is not the place to get into the Braun...<br /><br />IMHO the LA63 is Panasonic`s miss. If you are willing to spend this much on a shaver, go the extra mile and get the LV61.<br /><br /> --The 5-blade LV61 is Panasonic`s crown jewel. Everything about it speaks of quality, ergonomics and careful execution. The handle feels solid, strong and comfortable. The head, while large, doesn`t feel out of proportion. The balance between the two is perfect. The head doesn`t feel as big as the LA63 because it is shorter in height even though it is broader from front to back to accommodate the five blades. The front to back pivot is much better damped so everything feels tight and right. As mentioned earlier, the trimmer is, unfortunately, the same as the LA63 and a little too short, making it difficult to see what you are doing because of the big head partly obstructing your view.<br />Now about the 5 blades. Like almost all shavers these days there is a center cutting strip (which Panny calls slit foil) in the middle. The two auxiliary blades are located at the outside extremes of the screen.<br />The one in front is the finishing foil and in back is the lift-tech foil. On each side of the slit foil are the main shaver blocks which are<br />fitted in traditional fashion to the top of the shaver inside. The other three blades are built into the screen.<br />To ensure the main cutters would not cause the head to be impossibly deep from front to back, they have been reduced in width considerably from those used on other models. That means less main cutter contact than others and makes you wonder how this thing can cut so well. I guess the other three blades actually do more than you might think. Frankly, when I first noticed this, I was completely taken aback. But, believe me, it works great. To give you a better idea of how this blade configuration may work on your face, I find that on my upper lip only one main cutter and the lift-tech foil are doing the work because only two blades will fit, and on the area below my lower lip and above my chin, it`s one main foil and the finishing foil.<br /><br />IMHO this is the best electric shaver on the US market today. I rate the shave 5 stars and the shaver exceptional in just about every category including comfort.<br />If you have a tough or difficult beard or just want to own the best, search no further. This is the king of shavers.<br /><br />UPDATE: FEBRUARY 7, 2014 ***<br /><br />Since writing this review I've had occasion to try the 4-blade Panasonic LF51-A model and was very impressed with it. It delivers a no- nonsense close shave with reasonable comfort and easily wins my vote for best Panasonic 4-blade. It's meant to replace the venerable 8243A model but doesn't seem to be well-known. And it's currently selling on Amazon for an incredible $110! If you're not inclined to spend the extra $100 or more for the LV61-A (which for me is still the best of all shavers), you will likely be very happy with this model. As I said in my review of it on December 23, 2013 I sometimes cannot tell the difference in shave closeness between this and the LV61-A, although the latter is definitely more comfortable in terms of smoothness. Overall, I think the LF51-A is a winner and a real steal at it's current price.

  231. Let me start by saying that any shaver review can be a mixed blessing in itself. It's not even really down to personal preference of shaver, because it's not always a (frontal lobe) choice. I've uploaded a couple pics under Customer Images so people can see what they look like. One thing that is lacking, however, is some sort of base.   248. I expected a lot from a shaver that, as of this writing, retails for five hundred bucks. I must say I didn't quite get it. Opening the box, I was surprised how little was included...the shaver, a vinyl carrying case, and the power adapter. For the price of this shaver I would have thought a hard case or at least one made of leather would have been provided. A cleaning brush and a counter stand would also have been nice. When evaluating this shaver I compared it to the [[ASIN:B003V37Z9W Norelco 1250xcc/42 SensoTouch Shaver]] that converted me from a blade shaver. I shaved one half of my face with the Panasonic and half with the Norelco. I alternated which side I shaved with each shaver. Tests were done with one-, two-, and three-day growths. Just like other electric shavers, Panasonic tells you it will take up to 30 days for your face to \\"get used to\\" it. Panasonic also only gives you a 30 day money back guarantee so you pretty much must decide if you like before your face gets used to it. Norelco's 45 day grace period is more reasonable. This shaver comes with a two year warranty. While the Panasonic shaver looks top-heavy it is very balanced to hold. Like the Norelco, the Panasonic cannot be used with the charger plugged in. It only takes an hour to charge up. I like the flexible head, the digital readout telling me how much charge remains, and the locking power switch. Both shavers say you can use them with shaving cream, so about half the shaves were done dry and the rest after lathering up with [[ASIN:B00172WFZS Proraso]]. On multiple-day growth it pulled noticeably when used dry, but no more so than the Norelco. When used with shaving cream the shave felt very smooth. It is noticeably louder than the Norelco. The three heads of the Norelco cover more area than the rectangular head of the Panasonic, but this isn't really an advantage in real life. Panasonic tells you to shave with a back and forth motion, rather than the rotary motion most electric shavers tell you to use. That takes some getting used to. The head has a wide \\"margin\\" around it, making precision shaving a challenge. The wide large head is most noticeable when shaving under my nose or up to the edges of my sideburns, where I cannot get as close in either case. Shaving dry, I thought both sides were similarly smooth. When shaving with shaving cream the Norelco side was noticeably smoother to me. The trimmer is a lot better than the one on the Norelco. Cleaning: On pg.3 of the manual there is precaution about cleaning the shaver with hot water. Otherwise the only cleaning instructions are to wait for the \\"clean\\" indicator to come on. You use liquid soap and the \\"clean mode\\" to buzz it clean. The parts and accessories insert included with the shaver lists a cleaning stand and solution refills, similar to Braun's, but the manual makes no mention of it. The first time I took of the top off to rinse it out, I accidentally popped out one of the foils out of the head. It took several tries with Mrs. Boilermate's small hands and greater coordination to get it back in. This is a \\"minus\\" in my opinion. The Wife Test: It was a wash. Mrs. Boilermate said the Panasonic side was smoother than the Norelco side about a third of the time, and equally smooth about a third of the time. Conclusion: As of this writing, for the cost of one Panasonic shaver you could buy two Norelco shavers and still have money left over. For that money you get fewer accessories and a shorter money-back guarantee. You also get a shaver that shaves well, but not twice as good as the Norelco. Given a choice, I would opt for the Norelco.

  250. I had previously owned a Panasonic ES8243A. It shaved almost as close as a blade with no irritation, way superior to my old Norelco. But my suitcase was stolen (shaver included) and I opted for Panasonic's latest top of the line 5 blade model. No need for the more expensive ES-LV81-K with the cleaning unit since liquid soap and water worked just fine with my previous Panasonic. While my previous model shaved very close, this is the first electric shaver I've used that shaves as close as a safety razor with identical results after skipping a day, and no irritation! And I'm talking about both neck and face -- no stubble! This is a detailed description of how I get such close results: Before going to bed, I wash my face and neck with a couple drops of USkincare Awaken Foam Cleanser and USkincare Bamboo Polish (which is an exfoliating scrub). I just use the Bamboo Polish twice a week to avoid irritating my skin. Next, I apply a couple pumps of USkincare Moisture Control Lotion with Vitamin C. In the morning, I take a shower to moisten and hydrate my face. I don't wash my face because the natural oils help to lubricate the skin. Then I heat some water to 180º F while my shaving brush is soaking in hot water in the sink. When my electric kettle beeps, I pour the water into my Dirty Bird Pottery shaving scuttle (original style). I spend about a minute to create a good lather with Classic Shaving Cream (unscented) and a Rooney best quality badger brush. Then I spend another minute to thoroughly lather my face. Next I shave, detach the foil head, lightly rinse out the cutters, and lather my face again. When I shave my face a second time, I shave my neck, cheeks, and chin 90º from the first shave. Shaving just once does not give me a safety razor close shave. Then I remove the foil head and briefly rinse the cutters and foil, reattach the foil head, squirt on a couple pumps of diluted Dr. Bronners liquid soap on the foil, run the shaver at the automatic 20 second high-speed cleaning mode while rinsing my face with warm water, remove the foil head, rinse the blades at the automatic 20 second high-speed cleaning mode, rinse the foil head, and let air-dry. Next, I rinse my face with cold water to close the pores and towel dry. Then I spray USkincare Damask Rose Hydrosol Regenerating Toner on my face and neck, tap my face with my fingertips to spread the toner, and let it dry for a couple minutes. Next I use a couple pumps of USkincare Oil-Free Aloe Hydrant Gel with Green Tea and spread it across my face and neck. A good moisturizer is an important step to keep the skin moisturized. These products are relatively expensive when compared to drug store brands, but they last quite a while because I have to use only a small amount each time. Plus they're hypoallergenic, the shave is very close, and my face doesn't feel any irritated afterwards. I'm not into using shaving cream that's a petroleum derivative or other potentially harmful non-organic products on my skin. I never thought different skin care products made such a big a difference before using USkincare. Now let's get to a review of the shaver itself. I've only been using it for three months but am not concerned about the longevity since my previous Panasonic performed flawlessly for a couple years. My beard is on the thick side but my skin is sensitive. When I first began using the shaver, I was a little disappointed because my skin was slightly red for the first few days. But my skin seemed to adjust and after the first week and there was no more redness. Panasonic promotes this shaver as requiring less passes than my old model but I find little difference in the amount of passes required. The main difference is in the closeness of the shave and zero irritation. I've never used this shaver dry. I've used my previous Panasonic wet/dry shaver dry a few times and preferred it wet. Since I have a shaver that takes advantage of the benefits of wet shaving, it makes no sense to not use a high quality shaving cream. The LED light on this newer model is brighter, so I can see it clearly even in a brightly lit room. At first, the foil head seemed huge but with the pivoting feature, it feels great on my face. The shaver felt almost too light when I started using it but now I appreciate how little it weighs. Ergonomics are perfect. I don't find myself accidentally pushing the power switch and the power lock is a clever feature for travel. And the noise level is quite low. I don't use the trimmer feature so I can't comment on it. The replacement cutter and foil combo sells for around $50. The cutters and foil head on my stolen Panasonic were almost ready for replacement after two years so I expect the new ones to last just as long. Panasonic recommends replacing the foil head once a year and the cutters once every other year as a general guideline. Conclusion: Yes, it's expensive, but what you're getting is a very high quality marvel of engineering that will give you the closest, most comfortable electric shave possible. It's something you will use and appreciate every day or can get away with using every other day. And it will put a smile on your face. Is it worth the money? Hell yes! This shaver is flawless. Cons: There is no stand for the razor so that it can rest vertically and take up less shelf space. It would also look nicer on a stand. Panasonic should design and offer a stand with a clip or something to hold the foil head while it's drying after cleaning. And something like a neoprene travel case would be a nice touch rather than an ordinary vinyl case, given this is a premium shaver at a premium price.

Good on the face, fair on the neck and as for head shaving let's just say it's the most expensive \\"pre-shave\\" on the planet. The razor is gorgeous, the cleaning station a technological marvel. But it's soap based and unlike the alcohol based Braun Clean & renew it causes buildup and doesn't strip the blades clean. Braun still has the best cleaning system bar none. Prior to purchasing the panny ES-LV61 I had considered upgrading to the SensoTouch 1280, however both models use the same replacement - scratch that idea.<br /><br />The 5 blade Panasonic ES-LV61K Arc 5 Multi Flex Wet/Dry<br /><br />If you're on the fence about this razor and still suffering through this review, let me assure you this is one spectacular machine. Right out of the box with a dry shave it's cuts as close and as comfortable - not to mention crazy fast, as the Braun did before it's fall from grace.<br /><br />The Arch isn't as dramatic so head shaving is not only comfortable as all the foils float - but it's incredibly effective.<br /><br />The center lift foil must have been inspired by the original and now defunct Braun Smart Foil, it lifts every single whisker no matter where, no matter how difficult and really does cut below the skin line for a blade quality shave.<br /><br />Of course you have to stretch your skin a bit in troublesome areas to help the 5 blade system work, it pulls the hairs with lightening speed - it's painless by the way there's absolutely no sense of pulling or burn.<br /><br />Just a cool, comfortable straight razor, Barber shop quality shave.<br /><br />Quick Specs And Observations<br /><br />* Just as German Engineering is most always top shelf, Japanese knives and blades are second to none. Panasonic Nano blades are forged steel and surgical quality sharp.<br /><br />* Multi Flex pivoting 360 degree patented head just does what it promises. It conforms to every single angle and curve with a definitive hug.<br /><br />Difficult areas such as under my jaw line and throat where I would need multiple passes and often a blade touch up - are history. One pass, perhaps two and the shave is baby butt smooth.<br /><br />* Hands down the most powerful motor there is at a whopping 14,000 CPM<br /><br />* Patented 5 blade cutting system - really does an amazing job<br /><br />* 45 minutes to an hour of shave time per charge<br /><br />* 5 minute quick charge<br /><br />* Crazy fast 14,000 cycles per minute (cpm)<br /><br />* Linear motor drive - surpasses rotary and pulse driven razors by miles. It's rapid fire fast and incredibly effective.<br /><br />* Micro thin foil is pretty amazing - but delicate and easy to tear. This is easy to avoid if you don't add pressure. Much like a straight blade or safety razor, let the weight do most of the work. The inclination to press hard is natural but try to avoid undue pressure<br /><br />* Can be used wet or dry. With creams or gels, perfect for a shave in the shower as it's 100% water proof.<br /><br />* Very good trimmer albeit hard to see due to the size of the head - but all electrics seem to have this issue to some degree. No sane person buys a razor for the trimmer, it is what it is.<br /><br />If you're still reading this Novel my hunch is your deciding between this razor and the ES -V81. I know I was. The poor reviews of the cleaning station, the soap based cleaning cartridges are problematic in my opinion.<br /><br />Both razors have an effortless sonic mode for manual cleaning. A little soap, press the button for sonic under warm water (never hot!) pop the foil off, rinse, viola it's like new.<br /><br />The ES-VI is black and has a few, I'm too old to say it but \\"cool\\" LED bells and whistles. Is it worth the extra $100 bucks - not for me, cleaning systems come with their own set of problems and added expense.<br /><br />On a lighter note, the ES-LV61 has a gorgeous aesthetic. The razor is a deep Indigo blue with metallic navy accents and a black rubber back grip.<br /><br />Perfectly balanced and surprisingly light and quiet - it's form meets function.<br /><br />While it's true that it takes between 3 and 4 weeks for your skin to get used to the razor, and the razors float system to get used to the contours of your face (and or noggin') the first shave from this bad boy was quite remarkable.<br /><br />If it was this impressive from the get go - it should get even better in time. The box comes with the razor of course, a manual, charger, nice quality soft carrying case and a plastic head protector.<br /><br />The razor is warranted for two years - make sure you register on line or mail in the registration card<br /><br />My past reviews of other electrics are somewhat more critical than complimentary. Not the case here. Elegant, efficient and powerful - this is the first electric I've used over the past 30 some odd years that does indeed deliver a comfortable, blade quality close shave.<br /><br />***UPDATE***<br /><br />As both my skin and the float system of the head have gotten used to each other - the shave has improved. Cleaining is a snap and re-confirms how glad I am to have passed on the cleaning station. I have always thought of using an electric for a wet shave to be somewhat of a gimmick - well I've given it a few tries and the expperiance is exceptional.<br /><br />In tradional, old school wet shaving there's a reason for the hot towels, the shaving brush and the rich dense creams. They all serve to break down and soften the whiskers which are made of Keratin which is quite dense and found in the enamel of our teeth as well. Soften the Keratin get a closer shave.<br /><br />I've been using King Of Shaves gel and the results have been outstanding. I still prefer the time saving elements of a dry shave but will tell you that a wet shave is even closer and faster.<br /><br />*** A FEW TIPS THAT MAY HELP****<br /><br />If your going to spend this much on a shaver and wet shave, even once in a while. I would urge you to never buy a can of edge, or for that matter most any shave cream that's sold in super markets and drug stores. An exception would be the before mentioned King of Shaves. An upgrade from KOS would be the British - Taylors Of Old Bond Street, one of the densist creams there are, the formula hasn't changed in hundreds of years - it's a remarkable product. It may seem expensive but a small tub will last you a year, the scents are superb and fade quickly. The best prices for either are big surprise, on Amazon.<br /><br />** Cleaning you new Panny - To get all the oil build up off the tiny nano blades soapy water isn't going to do it. So I figured if Dawn dishwashing liquid was good enough to clean up the horrific Valdez oil spill - not to mention save the lives of countless wild life it was worth a shot and it just so happened we had it in the house. Dawns patented grease and oil cutting properties, strip those nano blades slick clean. All you need is a drop, press for sonic clean (keep the foil on) rinse and viola it's a brand new day.<br /><br />Still hands down the best electric I have ever used it trumps my now defunct Porsche razor which was twice the price. Owch.<br /><br />Highly recommended.me, cleaning systems come with their own set of problems and added expense.<br /><br />On a lighter note, the ES-LV61 has a gorgeous aesthetic. After waiting an eternity for the price of the Panasonic LV-61 to drop (it never really did!), I took the plunge and purchased one instead of replacing the expired foil and cutter of my trusty old Panasonic ES8249K. With the new LV-61, I get an even closer shave than any of the prior models and suffer absolutely no irritation whatsoever. I thought the large head on the LV-61 would be a problem, but the shaver is light, is very comfortable to hold and the head size actually feels good against my head, face and neck. That's right, this shaver is great for head shaving too, and the larger head actually makes the shaver ideal for this purpose. I'm currently using this shaver with a single pump of Kiss My Face Moisture Shave mixed with a little water for the face, and a single pump for the head as well. I get a nice, smooth, irritation free shave with this combination of shaver and shave cream. LONG-TERM UPDATE: After about a year and a half of owning this shaver, I noticed the screen completely stopped working. The rest of the shaver worked just fine, but I could no longer tell how much charge was left in the shaver. As I approached the two-year mark on the Panasonic warranty, I contacted Panasonic and sent them the shaver for repair/replacement. About a week-and-a-half later I received a brand spanking new ES-LV61 via UPS! Panasonics may be a bit pricey, but the warranty support more than enough makes up for it. Hmmm. . . I wonder if the replacement shaver is also covered by a fresh 2 year warranty? :- )I then turn on the shaver's 20-second ultrasonic cleaning mode. Once the cleaning cycle has finished, I remove the shaver from the mug and allow any remaining shower cleaner to drain into the mug. I then remove the shaver head and give the shaver and head a few shakes to remove any excess cleaner. I then re-attach the shaver head and set the shaver down to air dry. (Alternatively, you could leave the head detached from the shaver to air dry if you have the space to do so.) When I go to shave again, I rinse the shaver under running water just to remove any residual shower cleaner immediately prior to shaving. I've found that this method completely eliminates the formation of soap scum that would normally develop on the shaver parts over time from shaving cream and liquid soap. It also helps to keep the shaver in like new condition and smelling quite nice. I actually prefer this cleaning method to the Panasonic Vortex I've had with some of the older models I've owned. You'll have to change your mug of shower cleaner every now and then, but a bottle of shower cleaner is a lot cheaper and will last a heck of a lot longer than those Vortex cleaning cartridges.<br /><br />WET SHAVING PRODUCT ADVICE HERE: I've used a number of different shaving creams, gels, solutions over my years of wet shaving with Panasonic shavers. I've tried Billy Jealousy Hydroplane, Jack Black Beard Lube, Aveeno shaving gel, various Edge and Gillette shaving gels, Noxzema Sensitive Skin shaving foam, Barbasol, Kiss My Face Moisture Shave, etc. The one I'm using exclusively now is Bump Stopper Medicated Shaving Gel by a company called High Time, which I normally get at my local Walgreens but I've seen is available here on Amazon ([[ASIN:B003NGN3A2 Bump Stopper Shaving Gel w/Aloe Vera & Tea Tree Oil, 5.3 oz]]). Once applied to the skin along with a little water, this shaving gel is clear and low foaming. It provides a very, very slick surface over which your shaver can glide. It also does not \\"gumup\\"/clog the shaver like most of the previously mentioned products, does not rinse/fall off of the surface of your skin, and gets even slicker with the application of a little water. Since it's clear, you can also see the spots you may have missed while shaving. It also has aloe and tea tree oil which are supposed to be good at reducing irritation and preventing the formation of shaving bumps. This is a great product and I can't recommend it highly enough for wet shaving with an electric shaver. It's also a fraction of the price of many of the previously mentioned products. Hope this helps.

Due to the additional blade, the head is larger than the prior generation of 4 blade shavers, but not so large that it can't be maneuvered well under your nose and around the contours of your face due to the multidirectional swiveling head (not just side to side, but also forwards and backwards as well as in and out). This shaver trims my facial hair more closely than my prior 4 blade Panasonic shaver, almost equal to a wet shave with a real blade. It takes a few hours before my hair grows out to appear the way it did immediately after shaving with my prior 4 blade Panasonic shaver.<br /><br />The twist lock feature on the power switch prevents accidental operation when traveling (packed in a suitcase or your gym bag). The charger plugs into the bottom of the shaver, 1 hour charge time. I don't miss the lack of a charging stand with this model.

  425. In my opinion, the money I spent purchasing the Arc 5 was worth every penny. For the last 30 days after arriving in the mail from Amazon, I have been getting unbelievably close shaves with very little or no irritation and/or hair bumps and it gets better everyday as my hair and skin adjusts to the routine. I am a black male in the military with very coarse beard hair and I could never find an electric razor that was powerful enough to shave my beard without having to press hard on my face and make several passes resulting in irritation and eventually razor bumps. I finally gave up on the electric razor and started using a Gillette Mach 5, only shaving with the grain. This method kept most of the irritation and razor bumps away, but I could never achieve that smooth, close shave I desired. 8 years have passed and out of nowhere, I started researching electric shavers again. It came down to the Braun 7 series and the Arc 5. After reading up on the Arc 5 shaver, I was convinced this was the shaver for me due to the wet/dry capabilities. I've tried both wet and dry methods and I must say that everything I read about this shaver is true and I am really enjoying the close, smooth shaves I get everyday.
